It's like cloud code at the at the center of of all your software we're working. Um and uh and that's very different from and and and basically every time you press any kind of button or uh anything in the app, it's actually sending a prompt to an agent. And that's very different from traditional software where uh the software is pre-built with rules uh that a programmer writes. Um, in an agent native app, uh, each feature is essentially a skill that the agent can do that has prompts and tools and all that kind of stuff and it runs in a loop until it's done. And there are new principles for how to build agent native apps. So, um, there's principles like par. So like whatever the agent can do through the UI, the the the whatever the user can do through the UI, the agent should be able to do. And you can see that in the way that proof works. So um granularity means um you want your you want this the the tools that the agent have has access to to be smaller than the features. So like an example of of granularity which is really interesting is um one thing that this app does not have yet is a clear all comments function. Uh, what I can do is I can say at proof, can you clear all of the comments here? Um, and look, there are no comments anymore. So, um, all right. So, what I'm going to show you is this thing called compound product. And again, I'm not going to like claim some like I created this idea and thought of it. This is really an evolution of of what everybody is doing. Um, and I've got a repo here. Um, and if the team could put this like, you know, in the chat um, or something, this is open source and you can use it. So, it's called compound product. Um, and I'm going to explain what it does. It's built on on Kirstson's idea of compound engineering uh Jeff Hunt's Ralph loop and then my implementation of Ralph loop. So I have a little a little a little graph um that I'm going to show you. Okay, so let me you can look at the graph for a second, but I'm going to explain first what are we trying to do. Um okay, so you probably are building a product or or an app or you're working on something and you want it to get better and better every day, right? And right now what you're probably doing is thinking of ideas to improve your product and then kicking off you know maybe a Ralph loop or maybe a PRD to go implement that idea right so the problem with that is that you are now the bottleneck right so you need to be thinking of the ideas to improve your app and then pro and then proactively going and building those things right and so what compound product does is basically does this in a loop automatically every every day. So what this does is you start at the top, right? So phase one, and if you're not doing this, this is like thing one you got to do. Um create a cron job every day that basically takes information from your database, from your app, from your users, basically what you would normally look at as like a marketing dashboard. um and and put that grab that data and then send off a request to Opus45 or GPT52 and say based off of this data, what is the one thing we should do, right? What's the problem that you see with with our acquisition or with our retention or whatever, right? And then write a markdown report, right? So now you have an agent's view of what is the one thing that you should be doing um to fix whatever is happening in your app and you have a markdown file and this should be happening automatically as a cron job at midnight right and so I do this right so right now I have a cron job that that pipes in information from our users from our free trial uh and then has open 45 write a report for me and then I get an email Right. And this email is packed with like valuable things like, oh man, you have a big hole in your funnel over here. You know, you should probably go fix it by doing this. And I was reading this report the other day and I'm like, why why don't I just automatically do whatever it suggested? This is kind of dumb that like it's waiting for me to say, yeah, go do it. So, this morning I built this and I'm I'm so excited to use it. Um uh and the way it works is it grabs this report, right? And then it takes that report and it runs uh and this is all done on bash, right? And this is going back to what I learned um through the Ralph loop. And the Ralph loop is not like a panacea and a perfect thing that fixes all the things, but there's a lot of value to bash scripts and bash loops because you don't run into context limits, right? And I would encourage you to think about using, you know, bash scripts and and loops a lot more and running your agent on your MacBook or, you know, uh locally to do that kind of stuff. Um, so I'm going to pause for a second, Karen. Am I making sense? Is there anything that's not clear? &gt;&gt; This sounds very logical. So the par principle says anything that the user can do in the app the agent can do. And because that's the way that you've architected notion, it makes it really easy to do this like integration where now you can use notion as this con conbon board with cloud code which you know you guys didn't initially set out to do that but you just made all these things available and not only is whatever the user can do through the UI the agent can do but it's also the tools or or the affordances the agent has are very granular. I think I think parody is really important and is something that um you know, I only joined notion in September and I think previously like there were previous iterations of notion AI, but the latest one, the notion agent, this is like a key principle is it should be able to do everything a user can do and that unlocks so much like emergent behavior. So, I think I I totally agree with that one.
